                                    </msub>
                                 </mrow>
                                 <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$$\begin{equation}{{E}_{soL}}\, = \,{{E}_{\left\{ {Li{{{({{H}_2}O)}}_x}{{{(EA)}}_y}{{{(Ac)}}_z}} \right\}}}\, - \,{{E}_{L{{i}^ + }}}\, - \,{{E}_{\left\{ {{{{({{H}_2}O)}}_x}{{{(EA)}}_y}{{{(Ac)}}_z}} \right\}}}\end{equation}$$</annotation>
                              </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(4)</span></div>Where <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/70e90504-8b6f-4dd2-9f56-ac1603090ee8/advs8189-math-0005.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:21983844:media:advs8189:advs8189-math-0005" display="inline" location="graphic/advs8189-math-0005.png">
                        <semantics>
                           <msub>
                              <mi>E</mi>
                              <mrow>
                                 <mo stretchy="false">{</mo>
                                 <mrow>
                                    <mi>L</mi>
                                    <mi>i</mi>
                                    <msub>
                                       <mrow>
                                          <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
                                          <msub>
                                             <mi>H</mi>
                                             <mn>2</mn>
                                          </msub>
                                          <mi>O</mi>
                                          <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
                                       </mrow>
                                       <mi>x</mi>
                                    </msub>
                                    <msub>
                                       <mrow>
                                          <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
                                          <mi>E</mi>
                                          <mi>A</mi>
                                          <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
                                       </mrow>
                                       <mi>y</mi>
                                    </msub>
                                    <msub>
                                       <mrow>
                                          <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
                                          <mi>A</mi>
                                          <mi>c</mi>
                                          <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
                                       </mrow>
                                       <mi>z</mi>
                                    </msub>
                                 </mrow>
                                 <mo stretchy="false">}</mo>
                              </mrow>
                           </msub>
                           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">${{E}_{\{ {Li{{{({{H}_2}O)}}_x}{{{(EA)}}_y}{{{(Ac)}}_z}} \}}}$</annotation>
                        </semantics></math>&nbsp;is the total energy of different solvation structures. <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/527125a4-3404-42c5-adc5-9eec114b2c54/advs8189-math-0006.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:21983844:media:advs8189:advs8189-math-0006" display="inline" location="graphic/advs8189-math-0006.png">
                        <semantics>
                           <msub>
                              <mi>E</mi>
                              <mrow>
                                 <mi>L</mi>
                                 <msup>
                                    <mi>i</mi>
                                    <mo>+</mo>
                                 </msup>
                              </mrow>
                           </msub>
                           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">${{E}_{L{{i}^ + }}}$</annotation>
                        </semantics></math> is the energy of the Li-ion. <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/f77ba263-b1dc-4b18-a355-8ddf0f77d737/advs8189-math-0007.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:21983844:media:advs8189:advs8189-math-0007" display="inline" location="graphic/advs8189-math-0007.png">
                        <semantics>
                           <msub>
                              <mi>E</mi>
                              <mrow>
                                 <mo stretchy="false">{</mo>
                                 <mrow>
                                    <msub>
                                       <mrow>
                                          <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
                                          <msub>
                                             <mi>H</mi>
                                             <mn>2</mn>
                                          </msub>
                                          <mi>O</mi>
                                          <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
                                       </mrow>
                                       <mi>x</mi>
                                    </msub>
                                    <msub>
                                       <mrow>
                                          <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
                                          <mi>E</mi>
                                          <mi>A</mi>
                                          <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
                                       </mrow>
                                       <mi>y</mi>
                                    </msub>
                                    <msub>
                                       <mrow>
                                          <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
                                          <mi>A</mi>
                                          <mi>c</mi>
                                          <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
                                       </mrow>
                                       <mi>z</mi>
                                    </msub>
                                 </mrow>
                                 <mo stretchy="false">}</mo>
                              </mrow>
                           </msub>
                           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">${{E}_{\{ {{{{({{H}_2}O)}}_x}{{{(EA)}}_y}{{{(Ac)}}_z}} \}}}$</annotation>
                        </semantics></math> is the energy of other coordination molecules or ions in a solvation structure.</div>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="advs8189-sec-0160">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="advs8189-sec-0160-title"> Molecular Dynamics Simulations</h4>
                  
                  <p>The molecular dynamics simulations were conducted Forcite module in Materials Studio, employing the COMPASS III force field<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#advs8189-bib-0052" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs8189-bib-0052_R_d70897409e2212" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 52 - J. Phys. Chem. B">52</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> to elucidate the structural and dynamic behavior of the studied solution system. In the 100% ethanol solution, the composition is defined by the presence of 1713 ethanol molecules. Conversely, in the 80% ethanol + 20% H<sub>2</sub>O solution, the mixture consists of approximately 1371 ethanol molecules and 1110 water molecules. In the 100% H<sub>2</sub>O solution, there are 5550 water molecules exclusively. All the simulated component ratios are consistent with the experiment. A combination of optimization algorithms was first employed, comprising steepest descent, adopted basis Newton-Raphson (ABNR), and quasi-Newton methods. The convergence criteria for geometry optimizations were set at a maximum tolerance of 0.001&nbsp;kcal mol<sup>−1</sup> for the total energy and 0.5&nbsp;kcal mol<sup>−1</sup> Å<sup>−1</sup> for the force. To equilibrate the simulation system, NPT (constant number of particles, pressure, and temperature) ensemble simulations using the Andersen thermostat<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#advs8189-bib-0053" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs8189-bib-0053_R_d70897409e2228" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 53 - J. Chem. Phys.">53</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> for temperature control and the Berendsen barostat<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#advs8189-bib-0054" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs8189-bib-0054_R_d70897409e2233" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 54 - J. Chem. Phys.">54</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> for pressure control. The simulations were run for a duration of 500&nbsp;ps. For further conduct of the data collection, NVT (constant number of particles, volume, and temperature) ensemble simulations were performed utilizing the Nosé–Hoover thermostat<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#advs8189-bib-0055" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs8189-bib-0055_R_d70897409e2239" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 55 - J. Chem. Phys.">55</a>, <a href="#advs8189-bib-0056" class="bibLink tab-link" id="advs8189-bib-0056_R_d70897409e2239" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 56 - Phys. Rev. A">56</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> and were also executed for a total of 500&nbsp;ps. A 1 fs time step was employed for all dynamics simulations. The long-range electrostatic interactions were calculated using the Ewald scheme and atom-based van der Waals interactions with a cutoff distance of 12.5 Å.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="advs8189-sec-0170">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="advs8189-sec-0170-title"> Electrochemical Tests</h4>
                  
                  <p>The electrochemical performances of active materials were tested in the CR2032 coin cell. Typically, cathodes were fabricated by mixing 80wt.% of active materials, 10wt.% of carbon black and 10wt.% of polyvinylidene difluoride (PVDF) binder as well as appropriate 1-Methyl-2-pyrrolidinone (NMP) as a homogenous slurry, and then cast on aluminum foil and dried in vacuum at 120&nbsp;°C for 12&nbsp;h, the mass loading of active materials for each electrode was about 2&nbsp;mg cm<sup>−2</sup>. Na metal and glass fiber (GF/D) were employed as counter/reference electrodes and separators, respectively, to assemble the 2032 half-cells in an argon-filled glovebox, where the H<sub>2</sub>O and O<sub>2</sub> were &lt;0.01&nbsp;ppm. 1&nbsp;<span class="smallCaps">m</span> NaPF<sub>6</sub> in the mixture of propylene carbonate (PC), ethyl methyl carbonate (EMC), and fluoroethylene carbonate (FEC) additive with a volume ratio of 50:45:5 was adopted as electrolyte. The galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) and galvanostatic charge/discharge performance were evaluated on a Neware battery testing system in the potential range of 2.5–4.1&nbsp;V (vs Na<sup>+</sup>/Na) at 25&nbsp;°C. The GITT tests were conducted at a constant current of 0.1 C (13&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup>) for 900 s followed by a relaxation of 2700 s within the voltage window of 2.5–4.1&nbsp;V. Cyclic voltammetry (CV) curves were recorded on a Princeton Applied Research VersaSTAT 4 electrochemical workstation.</p>
                  </section>
               </section>
            </section>
         </section>
